Topic: Medicine
Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  High-density lipoprotein (HDL) is considered good cholesterol, and a level above 60 mg/dL is considered protective against heart disease. A level below 40 mg/dL for men and below 50 mg/dL for women is considered low.
  Low-density lipoprotein (LDL) is considered bad cholesterol, and a level below 100 mg/dL is optimal. A level between 100 and 129 mg/dL is near optimal, while a level between 130 and 159 mg/dL is borderline high. A level between 160 and 189 mg/dL is high, and a level above 190 mg/dL is very high.
  Triglycerides (TG) are a type of fat found in the blood. A level below 150 mg/dL is considered normal.
  Statins are a class of drugs commonly used to lower LDL cholesterol levels.
  Fenofibrate is a drug used to lower triglyceride levels and increase HDL cholesterol levels.
  
Analysis:
  The patient has low HDL and high TG levels, which are both risk factors for heart disease. The LDL level is not very high, but it is still above the optimal range. Therefore, the patient would benefit from a medication that lowers LDL, increases HDL, and lowers TG levels. Option A, Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate, is a good choice because it addresses all three lipid parameters. Option B, Fenofibrate alone, would only address the TG level and HDL level, but not the LDL level. Option C, Rosuvastatin 10 mg, would only address the LDL level. Option D, Atorvastatin 80 mg, would only address the LDL level and not the HDL or TG levels.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - Myocardial infarction is a condition where there is a blockage of blood flow to the heart muscle.
  - Lipid profile is a blood test that measures the levels of different types of cholesterol and triglycerides in the blood.
  - HDL is known as "good" cholesterol, LDL is known as "bad" cholesterol, and high levels of triglycerides can increase the risk of heart disease.
  - Statins are a class of drugs that can lower LDL cholesterol levels, while fibrates are a class of drugs that can lower triglyceride levels and increase HDL cholesterol levels.
  
Analysis:
  - The patient had a recent myocardial infarction and has abnormal lipid levels.
  - The preferred treatment in this case would be to lower the LDL cholesterol levels and the triglyceride levels.
  - A combination of a statin (to lower LDL cholesterol) and a fibrate (to lower triglycerides and increase HDL cholesterol) may be more effective in this case than either drug alone.
  - Atorvastatin 80 mg is a high dose of a statin and may be associated with a higher risk of side effects, especially in older patients.

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Knowledge:
The floor of the third ventricle is located in the middle of the brain and is formed by several structures, including the optic chiasm, the infundibulum, the mammillary bodies, and several cranial nerves.
A: The optic stalk is a structure that connects the optic nerve to the brain and is located on the floor of the third ventricle.
B: The third nerve (also known as the oculomotor nerve) is a cranial nerve that controls eye movement and is located on the floor of the third ventricle.
C: The infundibulum is a structure that connects the hypothalamus to the pituitary gland and is located on the floor of the third ventricle.
D: The mammillary body is a structure that is involved in memory processing and is located on the floor of the third ventricle.
Action: Answer("B") 
The third nerve is located on the floor of the third ventricle.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The third ventricle is a cavity within the brain, filled with cerebrospinal fluid (CSF), which is continuous with the lateral ventricles anteriorly through the interventricular foramen (foramen of Monro) and posteriorly with the fourth ventricle through the cerebral aqueduct (aqueduct of Sylvius). 
  A: The optic stalk, also known as the optic nerve, is a structure that connects the eye to the brain and passes through the floor of the third ventricle.
  B: The third nerve, also known as the oculomotor nerve, is a cranial nerve that controls the movement of certain eye muscles and emerges from the floor of the third ventricle.
  C: The infundibulum is a funnel-shaped structure that connects the hypothalamus to the pituitary gland and passes through the floor of the third ventricle.
  D: The mammillary bodies are a pair of small round structures located on the undersurface of the brain that are involved in memory and are located posterior to the floor of the third ventricle.
Action: Answer("D")

  D: Mammillary body is a pair of small round structures located on the undersurface of the brain.

Question: Short child with low T4 and raised TSH and swelling of pituitary, what is the diangosis ?
Choices:
  A: Primary hypothyrodism
  B: Pituitary tumor
  C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma
  D: TSH resistance
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  T4 and TSH are hormones produced by the thyroid gland.
  A: Primary hypothyroidism is a condition where the thyroid gland produces insufficient amounts of thyroid hormones. It can cause short stature in children.
  B: Pituitary tumor can cause abnormal growth hormone secretion and can result in gigantism or acromegaly, but not short stature.
  C: TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma is a rare type of pituitary tumor that secretes excess TSH, leading to hyperthyroidism, but not hypothyroidism.
  D: TSH resistance is a rare genetic disorder that leads to reduced sensitivity of thyroid gland to circulating TSH, resulting in elevated TSH levels and normal or high T4 levels. It can cause short stature in children.

Action: Answer("A") 

Based on the information provided, the child has low T4 and raised TSH, which is consistent with primary hypothyroidism. The swelling of the pituitary gland could be due to pituitary hyperplasia, which is a compensatory response to the low thyroid hormone levels.

Topic: Dental
Question: Which of the following show chemical bond with enamel (calcified tissues)?
Choices:
  A: Composites
  B: Direct filling resins
  C: Polycarboxylate cements
  D: BIS-GMA resins in pit and fissure sealants
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A: Composites are tooth-colored restorative materials composed of a resin matrix and filler particles. They bond to enamel through a process called acid etching, which creates micro-porosities in the enamel surface and allows the adhesive to penetrate and form a mechanical bond with the enamel.
  B: Direct filling resins are similar to composites and bond to enamel through the same acid etching process.
  C: Polycarboxylate cements are dental cements used for luting and bonding restorations. They bond to enamel through a chemical reaction with calcium ions in the enamel surface.
  D: BIS-GMA resins are used in pit and fissure sealants, which are preventive coatings placed on the occlusal (chewing) surfaces of teeth. They bond to enamel through a combination of mechanical retention and chemical bonding with the enamel surface.
Action: Answer("A") or Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Enamel is the hard calcified tissue that covers the outer layer of the tooth.
  A: Composites are a mixture of various materials, including resin and fillers, used to restore teeth. They bond to dentin, not enamel.
  B: Direct filling resins are used to restore teeth and bond to dentin, not enamel.
  C: Polycarboxylate cements are used to bond metal orthodontic bands to teeth, but they do not bond to enamel.
  D: BIS-GMA resins in pit and fissure sealants bond to the enamel of teeth, forming a protective layer against decay.
Action: Answer("D")

  The auditory cortex is located in the temporal lobe of the brain.

Topic: Dental
Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure that involves creating a flap of tissue adjacent to a tooth to gain access to the tooth's root and surrounding bone.
  Roots that have been denuded for a long period of time may have lost some of the periodontal ligament (PDL) fibers that normally attach them to the surrounding bone.
  A: The PDL fibers normally attach the tooth's cementum to the surrounding bone, so if the roots have been denuded for a long period of time, it is unlikely that PDL fibers would still be attached to the cementum.
  B: If the roots have been denuded for a long period of time, it is possible that some PDL fibers may still be attached to the tooth's dentin.
  C: When roots are denuded, the adjacent epithelium may migrate down the root surface, leading to the formation of a long junctional epithelium. This is a common response to denuded roots.
  D: Co-adaptation refers to the ability of the tooth and surrounding bone to adapt to changes in occlusal forces. While this is an important factor in the long-term success of dental procedures, it is not directly related to the presence or absence of PDL fibers on denuded roots.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - A lateral sliding flap is a periodontal surgical procedure in which the gum tissue is partially separated from the underlying tooth and bone in order to access and treat the underlying structures.
  - The periodontal ligament (PDL) is a group of specialized connective tissue fibers that attach the tooth to the surrounding bone.
  - The cementum is a specialized calcified tissue that covers the root surface of the tooth and provides attachment for the PDL fibers.
  - Dentin is the hard, calcified tissue that forms the bulk of the tooth structure.
  - Epithelium refers to the tissue that covers the outer surface of the body and lines the internal organs.
  
Answer: 
  Based on the given choices, the most likely answer is C because when roots are denuded for a prolonged period of time, the underlying root surface becomes covered by a layer of epithelial cells as a result of the body's attempt to heal the area. This layer of epithelium prevents the PDL fibers from reattaching to the root surface, which can compromise the stability of the tooth. None of the other choices accurately describe the expected outcome of a lateral sliding flap procedure on a tooth with denuded roots. 
  Action: Answer("C")

Knowledge:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure that involves cutting and raising a flap of gum tissue to expose the root of a tooth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the root surface has been exposed for 6 years.
  A: PDL (periodontal ligament) fibres attach the tooth to the surrounding bone and cementum. If the cementum is present, the PDL fibres will be attached to it.
  B: Dentin is the hard tissue that makes up the bulk of the tooth structure. PDL fibres are not normally attached to dentin.
  C: When root surface is exposed, the epithelium migrates down the root surface, forming a barrier to protect the underlying connective tissue and bone.
  D: Co-adaptation refers to the process of the PDL fibres reattaching to the root surface after a surgical procedure.
Action: Answer("C")

  The PDL contains nerves, blood vessels, and connective tissue.

  C: Ganglion cells are the cells most commonly affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy. They are the cells that transmit visual information from the retina to the brain via the optic nerve.
  D: Rods and cones are photoreceptor cells that convert light into electrical signals that are then transmitted to bipolar cells. They are not the cells most commonly affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy.
Action: Answer("C")

Choices:
  A: TVS
  B: hysteroscopy
  C: Endometrial biopsy
  D: chromosomal abnormalities
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Preconceptual counseling is a medical consultation that helps identify and manage risk factors before pregnancy.
  Second trimester abortion is a pregnancy loss that occurs between 14 and 24 weeks of pregnancy.
  A: Transvaginal ultrasound (TVS) is a non-invasive imaging technique that uses high-frequency sound waves to produce images of the female reproductive system. It is commonly used to diagnose conditions such as uterine fibroids, ovarian cysts, and polycystic ovary syndrome (PCOS). 
  B: Hysteroscopy is a minimally invasive surgical procedure that allows doctors to examine the inside of the uterus using a thin, lighted tube called a hysteroscope. It is commonly used to diagnose and treat conditions such as abnormal uterine bleeding, uterine fibroids, and infertility.
  C: Endometrial biopsy is a procedure in which a small sample of tissue is removed from the lining of the uterus and examined under a microscope. It is commonly used to diagnose conditions such as endometrial hyperplasia and endometrial cancer.
  D: Chromosomal abnormalities can cause pregnancy loss, birth defects, and developmental delays. Chromosomal testing can be performed on a blood sample or a sample of fetal tissue to identify chromosomal abnormalities.
 
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:

  B: Hysteroscopy is a procedure in which a thin, lighted tube called a hysteroscope is inserted into the vagina to examine the cervix and inside of the uterus. Hysteroscopy can be used to diagnose and treat a variety of gynecological conditions.
  C: Endometrial biopsy is a procedure in which a small sample of tissue is taken from the lining of the uterus and examined under a microscope. Endometrial biopsy can be used to diagnose a variety of gynecological conditions, including abnormal uterine bleeding and endometrial cancer.
  D: Chromosomal abnormalities can cause pregnancy loss or birth defects. Chromosomal abnormalities can be detected by various tests, including karyotyping and chromosomal microarray analysis (CMA).

  B: Type 2 root canal systems have two canals that join into one before exiting at the root tip.

  Type I: C-shaped canal with a single orifice and a single main canal.

- The stage 5 CKD is the end-stage of renal disease, where there is a significant decrease in the glomerular filtration rate (GFR) to less than 15 mL/min/1.73 m.
- Type 2 diabetes mellitus is a chronic metabolic disease that affects the body's ability to metabolize glucose.
- Injectable insulin is usually used in patients who cannot control their blood glucose levels with oral hypoglycemic agents.
- The oral hypoglycemic agents should be used with caution in CKD patients, and their dose should be adjusted according to their renal function.
- Linagliptin, Vildagliptin, and Sitagliptin are DPP-4 inhibitors that can be used in patients with CKD, and they do not require dose adjustment.
- Repaglinide is a meglitinide that should be avoided in patients with CKD, especially those with end-stage renal disease (ESRD), due to its active metabolites' accumulation and prolonged hypoglycemic effect.
- Glimepiride is a sulfonylurea that should be used with caution in patients with CKD, especially those with ESRD, due to its active metabolites' accumulation and prolonged hypoglycemic effect.

Action: Answer("A")  
Linagliptin is a DPP-4 inhibitor that can be used in patients with CKD, and it does not require dose adjustment.

Topic: Social & Preventive Medicine
Question: A 10-year boy with dog bite unprovoked comes to you. Appropriate action is:
Choices:
  A: Give cell culture derived vaccine
  B: Withhold vaccine and observe dog for 10 days
  C: Kill dog and send brain for biopsy
  D: No fuher action is necessary
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Dog bite can lead to the transmission of rabies virus, which is fatal in humans if not treated in time.
  A: Cell culture derived vaccine is an appropriate prophylactic measure in case of suspected rabies exposure.
  B: Observing the dog for 10 days is an appropriate measure if the dog is healthy and available for observation. However, it is not appropriate to withhold vaccine in case of suspected rabies exposure.
  C: Killing the dog and sending the brain for biopsy is not an appropriate measure for suspected rabies exposure. It is a public health measure that is taken only if the dog has bitten someone and shows signs of rabies.
  D: No further action is not appropriate in case of suspected rabies exposure.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Dog bites can transmit rabies.
  A: Cell culture derived vaccine is given to individuals who have not been previously vaccinated against rabies and have been bitten by an animal suspected to have rabies.
  B: Observing the dog for 10 days is appropriate in situations where the dog is healthy, available for observation, and the bite is not severe.
  C: Killing the dog and sending the brain for biopsy is not recommended unless the dog is showing signs of rabies.
  D: Not taking any further action is not appropriate in situations where the bite is unprovoked and there is a risk of rabies transmission.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Dog bite is a common problem in many countries.
  Rabies is a serious viral disease that can be transmitted to humans through the bite of an infected animal, especially dogs.
  Rabies is almost always fatal once symptoms appear, but it can be prevented with a vaccine.
  The recommended action depends on various factors, such as the type of animal, the severity and location of the bite, and the vaccination status of the animal.
  
Answer: "A" 
Explanation: In this scenario, the boy was unprovoked bitten by a dog. The appropriate action in such a case is to give cell culture derived vaccine (also called post-exposure prophylaxis or PEP) as soon as possible. PEP is a series of injections that can prevent rabies if given before symptoms appear. It is important to start PEP as soon as possible, ideally within 24 hours of the bite, to increase its effectiveness. Withholding the vaccine or waiting for the dog to be observed for 10 days is not recommended, as this can delay treatment and increase the risk of rabies. Killing the dog and sending its brain for biopsy is also not necessary in this case, as it is not a stray dog and there is no evidence of rabies infection.
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  Dog bites can transmit rabies, which is a serious viral infection that affects the nervous system and can be fatal if left untreated. 
  A: Cell culture derived vaccine is a post-exposure prophylaxis against rabies. It is recommended for people who have been bitten by dogs or other animals that may carry rabies.
